Chapter 6
Conclusions and Future
Work
6.1
Conclusions
The objective of this thesis was to propose a Hybrid Economic Dispatch combining
robust optimization and stochastic programming. Subsequently results will be com-
pared to study how this Hybrid Economic Dispatch performs.
After solving the diﬀerent cases proposed, we conclude that the stochastic economic
dispatch model provides the best dispatch solution when the expected value of the
system cost realized. The robust economic dispatch model provides the best dispatch
solution when the worst-case system operating cost is realized.
Finally the hybrid
robust-stochastic model provides a dispatch solution that performs relatively well in
terms of the expected and the worst case system operating cost.
It was demonstrated that the k-means clustering method improves the dispatch solu-
tion compared to a randomly selection of the scenarios within the partitions.
Benders decomposition technique was applied in order to simplify the hybrid prob-
lem. The solution for the dispatch cost obtained in the Benders decomposition with
primal cut is the same as the solution obtained in the extensive form of the Hybrid
Economic Dispatch in the three cases of study. For the Benders decomposition with
dual cut the dispatch solution cost in the 14-node system case and the 72-node sys-
tem case diﬀer slightly from the solution obtained in the extensive form of the hybrid
==PAGE:108==
88
Conclusions and Future Work
model. Therefore, we conclude that Benders decomposition with primal cut and Ben-
ders decomposition with dual cut alternative methods which approximate the solution
obtained by the extensive form of the Hybrid Economic Dispatch.
The computational times obtained during the simulation of the ﬁve diﬀerent mod-
els have been studied. For small or medium cases with a large name of scenarios as
the 14-node system, the extensive form of the Hybrid Economic Dispatch needs less
computational time than the two Benders decomposition models. On the other hand
for big cases and less number of scenarios as the 72-node system, the two Benders de-
composition models, need less computational time to reach the optimal solution than
the extensive form of the Hybrid Economic Dispatch.
For the 14-nodes system case the Benders dual cut model needs more computational
time than the Benders primal cut model. On the other hand for the 72-nodes system
case the Benders decomposition with dual cut needs less computational time to reach
the optimal solution than the Benders decomposition with primal cut. We conclude
that the complexity of the 72-nodes system case forces the Benders with primal cut to
make more iterations, therefore the size of the problem becomes bigger increasing the
computational time. Hence, according to the results obtained, for cases with a large
number of data Benders dual cut model is the best choice. Furthermore, all the models
perform following the same behavior in all the case studies. This assumption means
that the all the models respond well for the three diﬀerent cases of study developed
throughout this thesis and we can assume that they are reliable models since there are
no inconsistencies.
The use of the Hybrid Economic Dispatch relies on how willing the decision-maker
is to assume certain risk. If the decision maker is willing to assume certain risk, the
best choice is the Stochastic Economic Dispatch. If no risk is to be assumed, then
Robust Economic Dispatch is the preferential choice. A compromise between these
two choices is the Hybrid Economic Dispatch.
6.2
Future Work
There is much room for future work on the economic dispatch models. The ﬁrst option
is to transform the economic dispatch problem in a unit commitment problem. A unit
commitment problem may provide solutions more accurate to the real operation of the
system since unit commitments problems include commitment status to start-up and
shut-down the diﬀerent units within the system. The second option concern ﬁnding
diﬀerent clustering methods to include the scenarios within the partitions and also
develop a new method to automatically select the optimum number of partitions to be
made. Another suggestion for future work is to compute the diﬀerent models partitions
in a parallel framework. This computation method would reduce computational time.
Finally the eﬀect of applying diﬀerent linear programming methods, in order to save
computational time, should be studied.

Appendix E
Complete Form of the
Economic Dispatch Models
E.1
Stochastic Economic Dispatch
In this section the complete formulation of the Stochastic Economic Dispatch is pre-
sented. This formulation covers a set of time periods t ∈{t1, ..., T}.Because this gen-
eral formulation allows for more than one single period of time there is a new kind of
constraints implemented (E.11)-(E.12). These constraints named ramping constraints
limit the capacity of production units within two consecutive periods of time, (E.11)
for ramping up and (E.12) for ramping down.

.. z =E= sum((g,t),C(g)*P(g,t)+Cu(g)*Ru(g,t)+Cd(g)*Rd(g,t)) + sum(
dynw,pi(dynw)*(sum((g,t),C(g)*(Pu(g,t,dynw)-Pd(g,t,dynw)))+sum((l,
